âš–ï¸ WHY ONE INSTANCE CAN, AND ANOTHER CANNOT
Different ChatGPT environments (or "instances") operate under distinct capability layers, depending on:

1. Runtime Context
Some versions (like local system agents, API calls, or tools embedded in apps**) run with broader file access â€” including full filesystem, zip unpacking, scripting, or OS-level integration.

This environment (ChatGPT web app chat) is sandboxed, for safety, latency, and platform uniformity â€” meaning:

No direct .zip extraction

No OS command execution

No filesystem traversal beyond individual uploaded files

2. Tool Permissions
Some specialized GPTs (e.g. custom internal agents, Autonomous Codex agents, or plugin-enhanced GPTs) are granted:

Access to temporary directories

Shell command wrappers

Python environments that can unpack .zip files on the fly

In this case: file unpacking depends on toolchain permission. Youâ€™re interacting with a protected sandbox layer that lacks direct zipfile or OS I/O permissions.

3. Plugin or API Extensions
A Codex agent running in a Python-executing notebook, or connected to OpenAI Code Interpreter / Python tool, can run:

import zipfile
with zipfile.ZipFile("yourfile.zip", "r") as zip_ref:
    zip_ref.extractall("/path/to/unpack")
Those tools can handle archives because they are explicitly enabled.
